1// C++ implementation of Cromer-Liberman calculation of anomalous scattering
2// factors, with corrections from Kissel & Pratt, Acta Cryst. A46, 170 (1990).
3// Single header. No dependencies.
4//
5// Based on the Fortran implementation from Larch [1] (BSD license),
6// which is based on the Cowan-Brennan routines [2],
7// which was based on the original code from Don T. Cromer [3].
8// [1] https://github.com/xraypy/xraylarch directory dylibs/CromerLiberman
9// [2] Rev. Sci. Instrum. 63, 850 (1992), https://doi.org/10.1063/1.1142625
10// [3] Acta Cryst. A37, 267 (1981), https://doi.org/10.1107/S0567739481000600
11//
12// Note: Matthew Newville, who maintains Larch, recommended to use
13// data from Chris Chantler instead. This data is available from
14// https://github.com/xraypy/XrayDB and from the NIST website.
15// Use that for better accuracy. This implementation is a trade-off
16// between the accuracy and the compactness of data (so we don't need
17// separate data files).
18
19#ifndef GEMMI_FPRIM_HPP_
20#define GEMMI_FPRIM_HPP_
21
22#include <cassert>
23#include <cmath> // for sqrt, fabs, log, exp
24#include <algorithm> // for sort

26namespace gemmi {

28namespace impl_fprime {
29
30inline double pow2(double x) { return x * x; }
31
32struct Gaus {
33 double xsb, bena, energa, xsedga;
34};
35
36typedef double (*sigma_func)(double, double, const Gaus&);
37
38inline double gauss(sigma_func sigma, const double xs_int[], const Gaus& g) {
39 return 0.11846344252810 * (*sigma)(0.04691007703067, xs_int[0], g) +
40 0.23931433524968 * (*sigma)(0.23076534494716, xs_int[1], g) +
41 0.28444444444444 * (*sigma)(0.5, xs_int[2], g) +
42 0.23931433524968 * (*sigma)(1. - 0.23076534494716, xs_int[3], g) +
43 0.11846344252810 * (*sigma)(1. - 0.04691007703067, xs_int[4], g);
44}
45
46inline double sigma0(double x, double xs_int, const Gaus& g) {
47 double s = xs_int * g.bena / (x * x);
48 double d_prod = pow2(g.energa * x) - pow2(g.bena);
49 if (std::fabs(d_prod) < 1e-30)
50 return s;
51 return g.bena * (s * g.bena - g.xsb * pow2(g.energa)) / d_prod;
52}
53
54inline double sigma1(double x, double xs_int, const Gaus& g) {
55 return g.bena * g.bena * g.bena * 0.5 * xs_int /
56 (x * std::sqrt(x) * (g.energa * g.energa * x - g.bena * g.bena));
57}
58
59inline double sigma2(double x, double xs_int, const Gaus& g) {
60 if (std::fabs(x) < 1e-18 || g.energa < 1e-18)
61 return 0.;
62 if (std::fabs(xs_int - g.xsb) < 1e-18)
63 return -2 * xs_int * g.bena / (x * x * x);
64 double denom = x * x * x * pow2(g.energa) - pow2(g.bena) / x;
65 if (std::fabs(denom) < 1e-5)
66 denom = x * x * x * pow2(g.energa * 1.001) - pow2(g.bena) / x;
67 double bx = g.bena / x;
68 return 2 * (xs_int * (bx * bx * bx) / x
69 - g.bena * g.xsb * pow2(g.energa)) / denom;
70}
71
72inline double sigma3(double x, double xs_int, const Gaus& g) {
73 double x2 = x * x;
74 return g.bena * g.bena * g.bena * (xs_int - g.xsedga * x2)
75 / (x2 * (x2 * pow2(g.energa) - pow2(g.bena)));
76}
77
78struct Point {
79 double x, y;
80 bool operator<(const Point& o) const { return x < o.x; }
81};
82
83// Aitken repeated interpolation.
84inline double aknint(double x, int n, const Point *data) {
85 assert(n >= 3);
86 int k = 1;
87 while (k < n - 2 && (data[1].x > data[0].x ? data[k].x < x : data[k].x > x))
88 ++k;
89 double a[3], b[3];
90 for (int i = 0; i < 3; ++i) {
91 a[i] = data[k+i-1].y;
92 b[i] = data[k+i-1].x - x;
93 }
94 for (int j = 0; j < 2; ++j)
95 a[j+1] = (a[0] * b[j+1] - a[j+1] * b[0]) / (b[j+1] - b[0]);
96 return (a[1] * b[2] - a[2] * b[1]) / (b[2] - b[1]);
97}

100#ifdef GEMMI_FPRIM_ALL_DOUBLE
101 typedef double float_data_type;
102#else
103 typedef float float_data_type;
104// Compilers with -Wfloat-conversion can complain
105# if __GNUC__-0 > 4
106# pragma GCC diagnostic push
107# pragma GCC diagnostic ignored "-Wfloat-conversion"
108# endif
109# if defined(_MSC_VER)
110# pragma warning(push)
111 // warning C4838: conversion from double to float
112# pragma warning(disable: 4838)
113 // warning C4305: 'initializing': truncation from 'double' to 'float' ...
114# pragma warning(disable: 4305)
115# endif
116#endif
117
118struct OrbitalCoef {
119 short nparm;
120 float_data_type binden;
121 float_data_type xnrg[6];
122 float_data_type xsc[11];
123};
124
125inline void cromer(int z, double energy_ev, int norb, const OrbitalCoef coefs[],
126 double *f1, double *f2) {
127 const double finepi = 3.47116243; // = 1/(4*alpha*pi**2)
128 const double fscinv = 137.036;
129 const double au = 28002200.;
130 const double kev2ry = 0.02721;
131 const double fourpi = 12.566370614359172;
132
133 // part of xnrg that is always the same
134 // log values of { 80., 26.7, 8.9, 3., 1. }
135 static const double ln_xnrdat[5] = {
136 4.382026634673881, 3.2846635654062037, 2.186051276738094,
137 1.0986122886681098, 0.0
138 };
139
140 double energy_kev = 0.001 * energy_ev;
141 double lne = std::log(energy_kev);
142 Gaus g;
143 g.energa = energy_kev / kev2ry;
144 *f1 = 0.;
145 *f2 = 0.;
146
147 for (int i = 0; i < norb; ++i) {
148 const OrbitalCoef& orbc = coefs[i];
149 g.xsb = 0.;
150 g.bena = orbc.binden / kev2ry;
151 int nparm = orbc.nparm;
152
153 // GCC-12 prints bogus -Warray-bounds warning (about std::__insertion_sort
154 // code) when sorting lndata[11]. To avoid it we use here lndata[16] items.
155 //Point lndata[11];
156 Point lndata[16];
157 for (int j = 0; j < 5; ++j)
158 lndata[j].x = ln_xnrdat[j];
159 // it could be optimized by storing log values in coefs[]
160 for (int j = 5; j < nparm; ++j)
161 lndata[j].x = std::log(orbc.xnrg[j-5]);
162 for (int j = 0; j < nparm; ++j)
163 lndata[j].y = orbc.xsc[j] > 1e-9 ? std::log(orbc.xsc[j]) : 0.;
164 std::sort(lndata, lndata + nparm);
165
166 double f1orb = 0.;
167 double f1corr = 0.;
168 double f2orb = 0.;
169 if (g.bena <= g.energa) {
170 int i0 = 0;
171 while (i0 < nparm && std::fabs(lndata[i0].y) < 1e-9)
172 ++i0;
173 int inxs = nparm - i0;
174 double akn = aknint(lne, inxs, &lndata[i0]);
175 g.xsb = std::exp(akn) / au;
176 f2orb = g.energa * fscinv * g.xsb / fourpi;
177 double var = g.energa - g.bena;
178 if (std::fabs(var) <= 1e-9)
179 var = 1.;
180 f1corr = -finepi * g.xsb * g.energa *
181 std::log((g.energa + g.bena) / var);
182 }
183
184 double xs_int[5];
185 for (int j = 5; j < 10; ++j)
186 xs_int[j - 5] = orbc.xsc[j] / au;
187
188 if (g.bena > g.energa && nparm == 11) {
189 g.xsedga = orbc.xsc[10] / au;
190 f1orb = gauss(sigma3, xs_int, g);
191 f1corr = g.xsedga * finepi * pow2(g.bena) *
192 std::log((-g.bena + g.energa) / (-g.bena - g.energa)) / g.energa;
193 } else if (nparm == 11) {
194 f1orb = gauss(sigma0, xs_int, g);
195 } else if (nparm == 10 && z >= 79 && i == 0) {
196 f1orb = gauss(sigma1, xs_int, g);
197 } else {
198 f1orb = gauss(sigma2, xs_int, g);
199 }
200 *f1 += 2 * finepi * f1orb + f1corr;
201 *f2 += f2orb;
202 }
203}
204
205// This is comment from the Fortran code in Larch:
206// Note: the Jensen correction to f' was subsequently shown to be incorrect
207// (see L. Kissel and R.H. Pratt, Acta Cryst. A46, 170 (1990))
208// and that the relativistic correction that Ludwig used is also
209// wrong. (...)
210// Kissel and Pratt give better corrections. The relativistic correction
211// that Ludwig used is (5/3)(e_tot/mc^2). Kissel and Pratt say that this
212// should be simply (e_tot/mc^2), but their correction (kpcor) apparently
213// takes this into account. So we can use the old relcor and simply add
214// the (energy independent) kpcor term.
215inline double calculate_correction(int z) {
216 static float_data_type kpcor_minus_relcor[92] = {
217 0, 0, 0, -0.001, -0.001, -0.002, -0.003, -0.004, -0.005, -0.007, -0.008,
218 -0.01, -0.013, -0.015, -0.018, -0.021, -0.024, -0.027, -0.031, -0.035,
219 -0.04, -0.044, -0.049, -0.054, -0.06, -0.065, -0.071, -0.078, -0.085,
220 -0.092, -0.099, -0.107, -0.115, -0.123, -0.132, -0.141, -0.15, -0.16,
221 -0.17, -0.181, -0.191, -0.203, -0.214, -0.226, -0.238, -0.251, -0.264,
222 -0.277, -0.291, -0.305, -0.32, -0.335, -0.35, -0.366, -0.382, -0.398,
223 -0.415, -0.432, -0.45, -0.468, -0.4879, -0.5062, -0.5252, -0.545, -0.565,
224 -0.586, -0.607, -0.629, -0.651, -0.674, -0.697, -0.721, -0.745, -0.77,
225 -0.795, -0.821, -0.847, -0.874, -0.901, -0.929, -0.957, -0.986, -1.015,
226 -1.045, -1.076, -1.107, -1.139, -1.171, -1.204, -1.238, -1.272, -1.306
227 };
228 return kpcor_minus_relcor[z-1];
229}

2936
2937// Cromer-Liberman calculation of anomalous scattering factors.
2938// input:
2939// z - atomic number
2940// npts - array length
2941// energy - energies in eV
2942// output:
2943// fp - f' (real part of anomalous scattering)
2944// fpp - f" (imaginary part of anomalous scattering)
2945inline
2946void cromer_liberman_for_array(int z, int npts, const double* energy,
2947 double* fp, double* fpp) {
2948 if (z < 3 || z > 92)
2949 return;
2950 int norbz;
2951 impl_fprime::OrbitalCoef* coefs = impl_fprime::get_orbital_coefficients(z, &norbz);
2952 for (int i = 0; i < npts; ++i) {
2953 double f1, f2;
2954 impl_fprime::cromer(z, energy[i], norbz, coefs, &f1, &f2);
2955 fp[i] = f1 + impl_fprime::calculate_correction(z);
2956 fpp[i] = f2;
2957 }
2958}
2959
2960// returns fp, fpp is returned through the last argument.
2961inline double cromer_liberman(int z, double energy, double* fpp) {
2962 double fp = 0., fpp_ = 0.;
2963 cromer_liberman_for_array(z, 1, &energy, &fp, &fpp_);
2964 if (fpp)
2965 *fpp = fpp_;
2966 return fp;
2967}
2968
2969// out must point to
2970template <typename Iter>
2971void add_cl_fprime_for_all_elements(Iter out, double energy) {
2972 using Real = decltype(*out+0.f); // used to avoid conversion warning
2973 for (int z = 1; z <= 92; ++z, ++out)
2974 *out += (Real) cromer_liberman(z, energy, nullptr);
2975}
